<div align="right"><strong>Exhibit 99.1</strong></div><BR><br>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>SILVERCORP METALS INC.<BR></B><B>Suite 1378 
&#8211; 200 Granville Street <BR>Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada V6C 
1S4<BR></B><B><BR>NOTICE OF ANNUAL GENERAL MEETING OF SHAREHOLDERS</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B>NOTICE IS HEREBY GIVEN </B>that the Annual 
General Meeting of the Company&#8217;s Shareholders be called and shall be held 
<B>at the offices of Silvercorp Metals Inc. </B>located at <B>Suite 1378-200 
Granville Street, Vancouver, British Columbia, V6C 1S4, Canada, </B>on 
<B>Friday, September 20, 2013 at 10:00a.m (Vancouver time)</B>, and at any 
adjournment or postponement thereof, for the following purposes:</P>
<TABLE style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman'" cellSpacing=0 
width="100%" border=0>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="4%">1.&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; </TD>
<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify>to receive the Report of the Directors;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="100%" colSpan=2>
<P align=justify>&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="4%">2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </TD>
<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify>to receive the audited financial statements of the Company 
for the year ended March 31, 2013, together with the report of the auditor 
thereon;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="100%" colSpan=2>
<P align=justify>&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="4%">3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </TD>
<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify>to fix the number of Directors at seven (7);</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="100%" colSpan=2>
<P align=justify>&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="4%">4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </TD>
<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify>to elect Directors of the Company for the ensuing 
year;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="100%" colSpan=2>
<P align=justify>&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="4%">5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </TD>
<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify>to re-appoint Deloitte LLP, Chartered Accountants, as 
auditor for the Company for the ensuing year and to authorize the Directors to 
fix the auditor&#8217;s remuneration; and</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="100%" colSpan=2>
<P align=justify>&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR>
<TD vAlign=top width="4%">6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </TD>
<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify>to transact such other business as may properly be brought 
before the Meeting or at any adjournments thereof.</P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Only Shareholders of record on August 16, 2013, 
are entitled to receive notice of and vote at the Meeting.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Shareholders are entitled to vote at the Meeting 
either in person or by proxy. Shareholders who are unable to attend the Meeting 
are requested to read, complete, sign, date and return the enclosed form of 
Proxy and deliver it to the Company&#8217;s Transfer Agent, <B>Computershare 
Investor Services Inc.</B>, in accordance with the instructions set out in the 
form of Proxy and the Circular accompanying this Notice.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B>DATED </B>at the City of Vancouver, in the 
Province of British Columbia, this 16<SUP>h </SUP>day of August, 2013.</P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: left"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>The information in this 
Information Circular is given as at August 16, 2013</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>This Information Circular is 
furnished in connection with the solicitation of proxies by the management (the 
</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>&#8220;Management&#8221;</FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>) of SILVERCORP METALS INC. (the </FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8220;Company&#8221;</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>), for use at 
the Annual General Meeting (the </FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8220;Meeting&#8221;</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>) of the 
shareholders of the Company, to be held at the time and place and for the 
purposes set forth in the accompanying Notice of Meeting and at any adjournments
thereof.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>In this Information Circular,
references to &#8220;the Company&#8221;, &#8220;we&#8221; and &#8220;our&#8221; 
refer to SILVERCORP METALS INC</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>. </FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8220;Common Shares&#8221; means common shares without par value 
in the capital of the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>SOLICITATION OF 
PROXIES</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>This solicitation is made on 
behalf of Management of the Company. Solicitation of proxies will be conducted 
by mail, and may be supplemented by telephone or other personal contact to be 
made without special compensation by directors, officers, and employees of the 
Company or by the Company&#8217;s registrar and transfer agent. All costs of 
solicitation will be borne by the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Unless the context otherwise 
requires, references herein to &#8220;Silvercorp&#8221; mean the Company and its
subsidiaries. The principal executive office of the Company is located at Suite 
1378 &#8211; 200 Granville Street, Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada, V6C 1S4.
The telephone number is (604) 669-9397, toll free telephone number is 1-888-224-
1881, and the facsimile number is (604) 669-9387. The Company&#8217;s website 
address is </FONT><U><FONT color=#353535>www.silvercorp.ca</FONT></U><FONT 
color=#101010>. The information on that website is not incorporated by reference
into this Information Circular. The registered and records office of the Company
is located at Suite 1378 &#8211; 200 Granville Street, Vancouver, British 
Columbia, Canada, V6C 1S4.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Unless otherwise indicated, 
all currency amounts stated in this Information Circular are stated in the 
lawful currency of the United States.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>PROXY 
INSTRUCTIONS</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><FONT color=#101010>Appointment of 
Proxyholder(s)</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The persons named in the 
accompanying form of proxy (the &#8220;Proxy&#8221;) are Directors and/or 
Officers of the Company. A Registered Shareholder (as defined below) has the 
right to appoint a different person or company, who need not be a shareholder, 
to represent the Registered Shareholder at the Meeting by striking out the names
of the persons</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>1</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_2"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%;%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>named in the Proxy and 
inserting the name of that other person or company in the blank space provided. 
If you leave the space on the Proxy blank, those Directors and/or Officers named
on the Proxy are appointed to act as your proxyholder.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Proxy must be signed in 
writing by the Registered Shareholder, or such Registered Shareholder&#8217;s 
attorney duly authorized in writing. If signed by a duly authorized attorney, 
the Proxy must be accompanied by the original power of attorney or a notarially 
certified copy thereof. If the Registered Shareholder is a corporation, the 
Proxy must be in writing signed by an officer or attorney of the corporation 
duly authorized by resolutions of the directors of such corporation, which 
resolutions must accompany such instrument.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>A Proxy will only be valid if
it is duly completed, signed, dated and received at the Company's registrar and 
transfer agent, Computershare Investor Services Inc. (&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Computershare</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;), in 
accordance with the instructions provided on the Proxy, not less than forty-
eight (48) hours (excluding Saturdays, Sundays and holidays) prior to the time 
set for the holding of the Meeting, unless the Chairman of the Meeting elects to
exercise his discretion to accept proxies received subsequently.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>REVOCATION OF 
PROXIES</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>A Registered Shareholder may 
revoke a Proxy by delivering an instrument in writing executed by the Registered
Shareholder or by the Registered Shareholder&#8217;s attorney authorized in 
writing, or where the Registered Shareholder is a corporation, by a duly 
authorized officer or attorney of the corporation, either at the office of the 
Company at any time up to and including the last business day preceding the day 
of the Meeting, or with the consent of the Chairman of the Meeting on the day of
the Meeting or on the day of any adjournment thereof, before any vote in respect
of which the Proxy is to be used shall have been taken. A Registered Shareholder
may also revoke a Proxy by depositing another properly executed Proxy appointing
a proxyholder bearing a later date with the Company&#8217;s registrar and 
transfer agent in the manner described above, or in any other manner permitted 
by law. A revocation of a Proxy does not affect any matter on which a vote has 
been taken prior to such revocation.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Only Registered Shareholders 
have the right to revoke a Proxy. Non-Registered Shareholders (as defined below)
who wish to change their voting instructions must, in sufficient time in advance
of the Meeting, arrange for the Company (where the Non-Registered Shareholder is
a </FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>NOBO </FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>(as defined
below)) or their Intermediaries (where the Non-Registered Shareholder is an 
</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>OBO </FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>(as defined 
below)) to change their vote and if necessary revoke their Proxy.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>HOW TO VOTE</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Only registered shareholders 
as of the Record Date (as defined below) (&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Registered Shareholders</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;) or 
their duly appointed proxyholders are permitted to vote at the Meeting. Non-
Registered Shareholders (as defined below) are not permitted to vote at the 
Meeting as only Proxies from Registered Shareholders can be recognized and voted
at the Meeting.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>If you are a Registered 
Shareholder you may vote by attending the Meeting in person, or if you do not 
plan to attend the Meeting, by completing the Proxy and delivering it according 
to the instructions contained in the Proxy and this Information Circular. If you
intend to attend the Meeting and vote your Common Shares in person, you do not 
need to complete a Proxy.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Non-Registered 
Shareholders: </FONT></I></B><FONT color=#101010>Most shareholders of the 
Company are &#8220;non-registered&#8221; shareholders (&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Non-Registered Shareholders</FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8221;), meaning the Common Shares they own are not registered in
their names but are instead registered in the name of the brokerage firm, bank 
or trust company through which they purchased the Common Shares. Common Shares 
beneficially owned by a Non-Registered Shareholder are registered either: (i) in
the name of an intermediary (an &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Intermediary</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;) that the Non-
Registered Shareholder deals with in respect of the Common Shares of the Company
(Intermediaries include, among others, banks, trust companies, securities 
dealers or brokers and trustees or administrators of self-administered RRSPs, 
RRIFs, RESPs and similar plans); or (ii) in the name of a clearing agency (such 
as CDS Clearing and Depository Services Inc. or The Depository Trust &amp; 
Clearing Corporation) of which the Intermediary is a participant.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>2</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_3"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%;%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>If you are a Non-Registered 
Shareholder, and unless you have previously informed your Intermediary that you 
do not wish to receive material relating to the Meeting, you should receive or 
have already received (i) from the Company or its agent a request for voting 
instructions or (ii) from your intermediary either a request for voting 
instructions or a proxy form. In either case, you have the right to exercise 
voting rights attached to the Common Shares beneficially owned by you, including
the right to attend and vote the Common Shares directly at the Meeting if you 
follow the procedures outlined below.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The documents that you 
receive, and who you receive them from, will vary depending upon whether you are
a &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>non-objecting beneficial 
owner</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221; (a &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>NOBO</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;), which means you have 
provided instructions to your Intermediary that you do not object to the
Intermediary disclosing beneficial ownership information about you to the 
Company for certain purposes, or an &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>objecting beneficial owner</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221; 
(an &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>OBO</FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8221;), which means that you have provided instructions to your 
Intermediary that you object to the intermediary disclosing such beneficial 
ownership information.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Non-Objecting 
Beneficial Owners</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>If you are a NOBO, a request 
for voting instructions from the Company or its agent is included with these 
materials. These securityholder materials are being sent to both registered and 
non-registered owners of the Common Shares. If you are a Non-Registered 
Shareholder, and the Company or its agent has sent these materials directly to 
you, your name and address and information about your holdings of Common Shares 
have been obtained in accordance with applicable securities regulatory 
requirements from the Intermediary holding Common Shares on your behalf. By 
choosing to send these materials to you directly, the Company (and not the 
Intermediary holding Common Shares on your behalf) has assumed responsibility 
for (i) delivering these materials to you, and (ii) executing your proper voting
instructions. Please return your voting instructions as specified in the request
for voting instructions.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>If you wish to attend the 
Meeting and vote in person, write your name in the place provided for that 
purpose in the voting instruction form provided to you and we will deposit it 
with our transfer agent, or, if you request on the voting instruction form, we 
will send you a form of legal proxy that will grant you or your appointee the 
right to attend the Meeting and vote in person. If you do not intend to attend 
the Meeting or have an appointee do so on your behalf but you wish your shares 
to be voted, please complete and return the information requested in the voting 
instruction form to provide your specific voting instructions. Otherwise your 
Common Shares will not be voted.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Objecting Beneficial 
Owners</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>If you are an OBO, you should
receive or have already received from your Intermediary either a request for 
voting instructions or a proxy form. Intermediaries have their own mailing 
procedures and provide their own instructions. These procedures may allow 
providing voting instructions by telephone, on the Internet, by mail or by fax. 
If you wish to vote in person at the Meeting you should follow the procedure in 
the directions and instructions provided by or on behalf of your Intermediary 
and insert your name in the space provided on the request for voting 
instructions or proxy form or request a form of legal proxy which will grant you
the right to attend the Meeting and vote in person.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The purpose of the above 
procedures is to permit Non-Registered Shareholders to direct the voting of the 
Common Shares of the Company they beneficially own. Should a Non-Registered 
Shareholder who receives one of the above forms wish to vote at the Meeting in 
person (or have another person attend and vote on behalf of the Non-Registered 
Shareholder), the Non-Registered Shareholder should strike out the persons named
in the proxy and insert the Non-Registered Shareholder or such other 
person&#8217;s name in the blank space provided. In either case, Non-Registered 
Shareholders should carefully follow the instructions of their Intermediary, 
including those regarding when and where the proxy or voting instruction form is
to be delivered.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>A Non-Registered Shareholder 
may revoke a voting instruction form or a waiver of the right to receive Meeting
Materials and to vote which has been given to an Intermediary at any time by 
written notice to the Intermediary. An Intermediary is not required to act on a 
revocation of a voting instruction form or of a waiver of the right to receive 
Meeting Materials and to vote which is not received by the Intermediary at least
seven days prior to the Meeting.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>3</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_4"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%;%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>VOTING OF SHARES AND 
EXERCISE OF DISCRETION BY PROXIES</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>If you complete your Proxy 
properly, then the nominee named in the accompanying Proxy will vote or withhold
from voting the Common Shares represented by the Proxy in accordance with your 
instructions on any ballot that may be called for and, if you specify a choice 
with respect to any matter to be acted upon, your Common Shares will be voted 
accordingly. If you do not specify a choice on any given matter to be voted upon
your Common Shares will be voted in favour of such matter or how the person 
appointed as your proxyholder sees fit. The Proxy grants the nominee the 
discretion to vote on amendments or variations to matters identified in the 
Notice of the Meeting and with respect to other matters that may properly come 
before the Meeting. If any such amendments or variations are proposed to the 
matters described in the Notice of Meeting, or any other matters properly come 
before the Meeting, your proxyholder may vote your Common Shares as he or she 
considers best.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>INTEREST OF CERTAIN PERSONS
IN MATTERS TO BE ACTED UPON</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Except as disclosed herein, 
no Person has any material interest, direct or indirect, by way of beneficial 
ownership of securities or otherwise, in matters to be acted upon at the 
Meeting. For the purpose of this paragraph, &#8220;Person&#8221; shall include 
each person: (a) who has been a director, executive officer or insider of the 
Company at any time since the commencement of the Company's last completed 
financial year; (b) who is a proposed nominee for election as a director of the 
Company; or (c) who is an associate or affiliate of a person included in 
subparagraphs (a) or (b).</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>VOTING SHARES AND PRINCIPAL
SHAREHOLDERS</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Company is authorized to 
issue an unlimited number of Common Shares, each Common Share carrying the right
to one vote. As at the date hereof, the Company has issued and outstanding 
170,781,058 fully paid and non-assessable Common Shares. The Company has no 
other classes of securities.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The directors of the Company 
have fixed August 16, 2013 as the record date (the &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Record Date</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;) for the 
determination of shareholders entitled to receive the Notice of Meeting and to 
vote at the Meeting. Any such shareholder who either personally attends the 
Meeting or has completed and delivered a Proxy in the manner and subject to the 
provisions described above shall be entitled to vote or to have his or her 
Common Shares voted at the Meeting.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>On a show of hands, every 
individual who is present as a Registered Shareholder or as a representative of 
a Registered Shareholder will have one vote (no matter how many Common Shares 
such Registered Shareholder holds). On a poll, every Registered Shareholder 
present in person or represented by proxy and every person who is a 
representative of a Registered Shareholder will have one vote for each Common 
Share registered in the name of the Registered Shareholder on the list of 
Registered Shareholders, which is available for inspection during normal 
business hours at Computershare and which will be available at the Meeting. 
Registered Shareholders represented by proxyholders are not entitled to vote on 
a show of hands.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>To the knowledge of the 
directors and executive officers of the Company, as at the date hereof there are
no persons who, or companies that, beneficially own, or control or direct, 
directly or indirectly, Common Shares carrying more than 10% of the voting 
rights attached to all outstanding Common Shares of the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>NUMBER OF 
DIRECTORS</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Management of the Company is 
seeking shareholder approval of an ordinary resolution to fix the number of 
directors of the Company at seven (7) for the ensuing year.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>ELECTION OF 
DIRECTORS</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The size of the board is 
currently fixed at seven (7) directors. Each director of the Company is elected 
annually and holds office until the next annual general meeting of the 
shareholders, or until his successor is elected or appointed, unless that 
person&#8217;s office is earlier vacated in accordance with the Articles of the 
Company or with the provisions</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>4</FONT></P></DIV><BR>

<BR>
<A name="page_5"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>of the </FONT><I><FONT 
color=#101010>Business Corporations Act </FONT></I><FONT color=#101010>(British 
Columbia) (the &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>BCBCA</FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8221;). Management has received written consent from all 
director nominees of their willingness and ability to serve as a director. The 
Company has adopted a majority voting policy in accordance with the 
recommendation of the Canadian Coalition for Good Governance, which means that 
any director nominee who receives more votes cast as withheld than voted in 
favour shall be considered not to have received support of the shareholders and 
will tender his or her resignation. In the absence of instructions to the 
contrary, the accompanying Proxy will be voted for the director nominees listed 
below. If there are more nominees for election than there are vacancies to fill,
those nominees receiving the greatest number of votes will be elected until all 
such vacancies have been filled.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The following table sets out 
the names of management&#8217;s nominees for election as directors, the

resident, all offices of the Company now held by each of them, each 
nominee&#8217;s principal occupation, business or employment, the period of time
for which each nominee has served as a director of the Company, and the number 
of Common Shares of the Company that each nominee beneficially owns, or controls
or directs, directly or indirectly, as of August 16, 2013.</FONT></P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>CORPORATE 
GOVERNANCE</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Company&#8217;s corporate
governance practices have been and continue to be in compliance with applicable 
Canadian and United States requirements. The Company continues to monitor 
developments in Canada and the United States with a view to further revising its
governance policies and practices, as appropriate.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The New York Stock Exchange 
(the &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>NYSE</FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8221;) rules require the Company to disclose any significant 
ways in which its corporate governance practices differ from those followed by 
United States domestic issuers under the NYSE listing standards. The Company 
believes that there are no significant differences between its corporate 
governance practices and those required to be followed by United States domestic
issuers under the NYSE listing standards.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The following is a 
description of the Company&#8217;s corporate governance practices which has been
prepared by the Governance and Nominating Committee of the Board and has been 
approved by the Board.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><FONT color=#101010>Board of 
Directors</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>In compliance with the 
requirements of the BCBCA, the directors are elected by the shareholders to 
manage, or supervise the management of, the business and affairs of the Company.
In exercising their powers and discharging their duties, the directors are 
required to act honestly and in good faith with a view to the best interests of 
the Company, and to exercise the care, diligence and skill that a reasonably 
prudent person would exercise in comparable circumstances.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Four out of six members of 
the Board are independent within the meaning of the Governance Guidelines and 
the independence requirements of the NYSE. To facilitate the ability of the 
Board to function independently of management there are only two members of 
management on the Board, the Chief Executive Officer and the President/Chief 
Operating Officer. During each board meeting the independent directs meet 
without the members of management present.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Board has adopted a 
description of how it delineates its roles and stewardship responsibilities in 
The Board of Director Charter, which is attached hereto as </FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Schedule &#8220;1&#8221;. </FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>This 
description incorporates the guidelines and principles outlined in 
</FONT><I><FONT color=#101010>National Instrument 52-110 &#8211; Audit
Committees </FONT></I><FONT color=#101010>(&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>NI 52-110</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;), </FONT><I><FONT 
color=#101010>National Instrument 58-101 -Disclosure of Corporate Governance 
Practices </FONT></I><FONT color=#101010>(&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>NI 58-101</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;) and 
</FONT><I><FONT color=#101010>National Policy 58-201 - Corporate Governance 
Guidelines </FONT></I><FONT color=#101010>(&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>NP 58-201</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;).</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Board believes that good 
corporate governance is important to the effective performance of the Company 
and plays a significant role in protecting shareholders&#8217; interests and 
maximizing value for the shareholders of the Company. The disclosure regarding 
the Company&#8217;s corporate governance practices that is required by NI 58-101
is set out in </FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>Appendix &#8220;A&#8221; 
</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>to this Information </FONT><SUB><FONT 
color=#101010>Circular</FONT></SUB><FONT color=#101010>.</FONT></P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>CORPORATE GOVERNANCE 
COMMITTEE</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Corporate Governance 
Committee is responsible for assisting the Board in establishing and maintaining
a sound system of corporate governance through a process of continuing 
assessment and enhancement. The Corporate Governance Committee works to ensure 
that the Board functions independently of management, that management is clearly
accountable to the Board and those procedures are in place to monitor the 
effectiveness of the performance of the Board, the Committees of the Board and 
individual directors. The Corporate Governance Committee is comprised of Paul 
Simpson, Earl Drake, and Yikang Liu, all of whom are independent directors 
pursuant to NI 52-110. The Corporate Governance Committee Charter is attached 
hereto as </FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>Schedule &#8220;2&#8221;.</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>COMPENSATION 
COMMITTEE</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Compensation Committee is
responsible for determining and approving compensation for directors and senior 
officers. The Compensation Committee is comprised of Paul Simpson, Robert 
Gayton, and Yikang Liu, all of whom are independent directors pursuant to NI 52-
110. The Compensation Committee Charter is attached hereto as </FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Schedule &#8220;3&#8221;. </FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>All 
committee members have direct experience in executive compensation. As a result 
of their education and experience, each member of the Compensation Committee has
familiarity with, an understanding of, or experience in reviewing executive and 
director compensation; administering of stock options and stock option grants; 
and reviewing performance goals and the assessments of executives. Within the 
last fiscal year, no consultants or advisors were retained to assist in 
determining compensation. The Compensation Committee did purchase the 2012 
Mining Industry Salary Survey compiled by a large international accounting firm 
to confirm the reasonableness of the CEO&#8217;s compensation package relative 
to other North American mining companies with similar revenues. The 
Company&#8217;s compensation policies and programs are designed to be 
competitive with similar companies and to recognize and reward executive 
performance consistent with the success of the Company&#8217;s 
business.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>AUDIT 
COMMITTEE</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>For information regarding the
Audit Committee, see the Company&#8217;s annual information form (the 
&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>AIF</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;) 
dated June 27, 2013, under the heading &#8220;Audit Committee&#8221;, including 
a copy of the Audit Committee Charter which is attached to the AIF as 
</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>Schedule &#8220;1&#8221;. </FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>The Audit Committee is comprised of David Kong, Robert Gayton, and
Earl Drake, all of whom are independent directors pursuant to NI 52-110. The AIF
is available under the Company&#8217;s profile at </FONT><U><FONT 
color=#353535>www.sedar.com</FONT></U><FONT color=#101010>.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Corporate Governance, 
Compensation, and Audit Committees will be re-constituted after the 
Meeting.</FONT></P>

completed financial years paid to the Company&#8217;s Chief Executive Officer,

officers, or the three most highly compensated individuals acting in a 
similar</FONT></P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Employment

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><U><FONT color=#101010>Dr. Rui Feng, Chairman, 
Chief Executive Officer and Director</FONT></U></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Dr. Rui Feng entered into a 
consulting agreement with SKN Resources Ltd. (the former name of the Company) 
dated May 1, 2003, to provide the following services: assisting in introducing 
Company management and personnel to Chinese geological personnel; assisting in 
reviewing and acquiring mineral properties in China; and assisting in 
negotiating agreements, including mining agreements. Dr. Rui Feng&#8217;s 
consultancy fee, as stipulated under the agreement was initially CAD$700 per 
day, plus applicable taxes, for each day services were provided to the Company. 
In addition, the agreement provides Dr. Rui Feng with Options, finder&#8217;s 
fees or bonuses, in amounts to be determined by the Board of Directors, for 
bringing mineral resource acquisition opportunities to the Company. All travel 
and other expenses incurred in connection with the provision of services are 
reimbursable. The initial term of the agreement was one year without any formal 
renewal provisions.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Dr. Rui Feng entered into a 
consulting agreement for two year term with Fortune Mining Limited (a subsidiary
of the Company) dated January 10, 2013, to provide the following services: 
assisting the Company&#8217;s mining and exploration development in China; 
providing senior executive services to the Company; providing management 
services to the company&#8217;s mining and exploration activities in China; 
presenting Company information and investor relations functions; reviewing mine
exploration and mine development information and related technical information; 
assisting in the hiring of senior management in China; assisting in reviewing 
and acquiring mineral properties in China; negotiating and reviewing agreements,
including mining agreements; and review mining permits and related exploration 
and development documents. Dr. Rui Feng&#8217;s consultancy fee, as stipulated 
under the agreement is $2,700 per day, plus applicable taxes, for each day 
services were provided to the Company. In addition, the agreement provides Dr. 
Rui Feng with options, finder&#8217;s fees or bonuses, in amounts to be 
determined by the Board of Directors, for bringing mineral resource acquisition 
opportunities to the Company. All travel and other expenses incurred in 
connection with the provision of services are reimbursable. Dr. Rui Feng&#8217;s
current billing rate is CAD$50,000 per month, as approved by the Board of 
Directors of the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Dr. Rui Feng is prohibited, 
during the term of the agreement and for a period of two (2) years thereafter, 
from acquiring any interest, direct or indirect, through associates or 
affiliates, in any exploration concessions, mining claims, leases, mining 
rights, interest in land, fee lands, surface rights or water rights within ten 
(10) kilometres of any property in which the Company has an interest at the time
of execution of, or acquires during the term of, the agreement. Under the 
agreement either party may terminate the agreement for any reason upon thirty 
(30) days written notice.</FONT></P>

dated March 1, 2004, to provide services ancillary to the office of President by
a company customarily listed on the TSX Venture Exchange.</FONT></P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Change of Control
Agreements</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Company has entered into 
Change of Control Agreements with each of Dr. Rui Feng, Myles Gao, Shaoyang 
Shen, Maria Tang, and Peter Torn. The terms of the Change of Control Agreements 
provide that if an executive officer&#8217;s employment agreement or consulting 
agreement, as applicable, is terminated, other than for cause, within 18 months 
after a Change of Control, the executive officer shall be entitled to a lump sum
payment equal to 18 months base compensation plus other sums owed for arrears of
compensation and if awarded, bonus, continuation of benefits for 18 months and 
immediate vesting of all outstanding Options.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Change of Control 
Agreements deem a &#8220;Change of Control&#8221; to occur if: (i) a merger, 
amalgamation, arrangement, consolidation, reorganization or transfer takes place
in which equity securities of the Company possessing more than 50% of the total 
voting power of the Company are acquired by a person or persons different from 
the persons holding those equity securities immediately prior to such 
transaction, and the composition of the Board of Directors following such 
transaction is such that the directors of the Company prior to the transaction 
constitute less than 50% of the Board membership following the transaction; (ii)
any person, or any combination of persons acting jointly or in concert shall 
acquire or hold, directly or indirectly, 25% or more of the voting rights 
attached to all outstanding equity securities; (iii) any person, or any 
combination of persons acting jointly or in concert shall acquire or hold, 
directly or indirectly, the right to appoint a majority of the directors of the 
Company; or (iv) if the Company sells, transfers or otherwise disposes of all or
substantially all of its assets.</FONT></P>

Company of related payments to the NEOs, (which includes the accelerated option 
based award value) is estimated at CAD$2,629,325</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>.

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><FONT color=#101010>Compensation Discussion 
and Analysis</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>16</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_17"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%;%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>During the 2013 fiscal year, 
total compensation paid to the Named Executive Officers has decreased to 
CAD$4,551,967 from CAD$5,687,734 in fiscal 2012 and increased from CAD$4,502,441
in fiscal 2011. During the 2013 fiscal year, total compensation paid to the 
Named Executive Officers changed primarily as a result of: (i) increase in 
payment of annual bonuses totalling CAD$1,138,800 compared to CAD$890,000 in 
fiscal 2012 and CAD$915,000 in fiscal 2011 and (ii) the value of stock option 
grants decreased to CAD$1,819,402 in fiscal 2013 compared to CAD$3,196,232 in 
fiscal 2012 and CAD$2,398,816 in fiscal 2011.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Company&#8217;s executive
compensation program is overseen by the Compensation Committee of the Board of 
Directors. See &#8220;Compensation Committee&#8221; above for a description of 
the composition of the Compensation Committee. The Compensation Committee is 
responsible for making recommendations to the Board with respect to the 
compensation of executive officers of the Company as well as with respect to the
Company&#8217;s stock option plan (the &#8220;</FONT><B><FONT 
color=#101010>Plan</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;). The Committee also 
assumes responsibility for reviewing and monitoring the long-range compensation 
strategy for the senior management of the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>In carrying out this mandate,
the Committee assesses on an annual basis the performance of the CEO, relative 
to both industry performance and overall Company performance, and compares total
compensation to compensation paid by comparable companies. Comparable silver 
mining and exploration companies continued to be comprised of publicly traded 
mining companies based of similar size, as determined by market capitalization, 
revenue, and complexity to the Company and include Eldorado Gold Corp., 
Endeavour Silver Corp., Exeter Resource Corporation, First Majestic Silver 
Corp., Hecla Mining Company, Pan American Silver Corp., Silver Standard 
Resources, Silver Wheaton Corp., and Taseko Mines Limited.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The objectives of the 
Company&#8217;s compensation program are to attract, hold and inspire 
performance by members of senior management in a manner that will enhance the 
sustainable profitability and growth of the Company. The Company has employed a 
combination of base compensation and equity participation through its stock 
option plan. In addition, the Company from time to time awards some of the 
executive officers, or companies controlled by executive officers, performance 
bonuses for the year. The Company does not offer securities purchase programs, 
shares or units that are subject to restrictions on resale or other incentive 
plans, and, except for Options, focuses on annual, rather than long-term, 
compensation.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Compensation Committee 
attempts to ensure that the compensation packages for executive officers and the
overall equity participation plan are in line with publicly listed mining and 
mineral exploration companies of a comparable size and with operations at a 
similar or a more advanced stage. The Compensation Committee does not rely on 
any formula, or objective criteria and analysis to determine an exact amount of 
compensation to pay. Compensation decisions are made through discussion by the 
Compensation Committee, with input from the CEO, with the final recommendations 
of the Compensation Committee being submitted to the Board of Directors for 
further discussion and final approval. The target is for the total compensation 
package granted to the CEO to be approximately in the middle range of other 
comparably sized mining companies; however, there is no fixed formula, or pre-
determined set of peer companies that is used for this determination.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Compensation Committee 
considered the implications of the risks associated with the Company&#8217;s 
compensation policies and practices and concluded that, given the nature of the 
Company&#8217;s business and the role of the Compensation Committee in 
overseeing the Company&#8217;s executive compensation practices, the 
compensation policies and practices do not serve to encourage any NEO or 
individual at a principal business unit or division to take inappropriate or 
excessive risks, and no risks were identified arising from the Company&#8217;s 
compensation policies and practices that are reasonably likely to have a 
material adverse effect on the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>No NEOs or directors are 
permitted to purchase financial instruments including forward contracts, equity 
swaps, collars, or like instruments, that are designed to hedge against a 
decrease in market value of securities of the Company granted to such director 
or NEO as compensation.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Base 
Compensation</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>17</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_18"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%;%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>In the Compensation 
Committee&#8217;s view, paying base salaries that are competitive in the markets
in which the Company competes for executive talent is a first step to attracting
and retaining talented, qualified and effective executives. The NEOs are paid 
salaries commensurate with those offered by other companies in our industry, 
with consideration also given to internal relativity and individual 
performance.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Short Term Incentive 
Plan</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Company does not maintain
any short term incentive plans for its NEOs but does award performance bonuses, 
as discussed below.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Option-Based 
Awards</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Company believes that 
encouraging its executive officers and employees to become shareholders is the 
best way of aligning their interests with those of its shareholders. The NEOs 
are granted options commensurate with those offered by other companies in our 
industry, with consideration also given to internal relativity and individual 
performance. Equity participation is accomplished through the Company&#8217;s 
Plan. Options are granted to executive officers taking into account a number of 
factors, including the amount and terms of Options previously granted, base 
compensation, performance bonuses, if any, and competitive factors. During the 
2013 fiscal year, the Board granted </FONT><FONT color=#101010>optionees Options
to purchase 1,520,000 Common Shares, representing 0.9</FONT><FONT color=#373737>
% </FONT><FONT color=#101010>of the outstanding Common Shares of </FONT><FONT 
color=#101010>the Company at year-end.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>All Options granted were 
granted at or above market prices, with a term of five years, and vesting in 
equal quarterly amounts over either a three or four-year vesting period. 
Suggested granting of Options is made by the CEO to the Compensation Committee, 
which considers the input of the CEO and then submits a recommendation for the 
grant of Options to the Board of Directors for final approval.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><I><FONT color=#101010>Performance 
Bonuses</FONT></I></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The NEOs are paid performance
bonuses with those offered by other companies in our industry, with 
consideration also given to internal relativity and individual performance. 
Considerations for NEOs performance bonus awards made during the fiscal 2013 
year were based primarily on three elements during fiscal 2012 (1) share 
performance; (2) Company performance, and (3) executive officers&#8217; 
performance. The Committee noted sales and profits and silver production in 
contemplating the bonus to award the CEO for fiscal 2012 performance.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Committee delegated 
authority to establish performance bonuses for other officers to the CEO and a 
total of CAD$388,800 in bonuses were awarded to all other NEOs in fiscal 
2013.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><FONT color=#101010>Performance 
Graph</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Common Shares of the 
Company commenced trading on the TSX on October 24, 2005, under the symbol 
&#8220;SVM&#8221; and prior to that time traded on the TSX Venture Exchange. The
Common Shares also trade on the NYSE, also under the symbol SVM. The following 
chart compares the total cumulative shareholder return for CAD$100 invested in 
Common Shares of the Company on April 1, 2007, with the cumulative total return 
of the S&amp;P/TSX Composite Index and S&amp;P/TSX Global Gold Index for the 
period from April 1, 2007 to March 31, 2013. The Common Share performance as set
out in the graph does not necessarily indicate future price performance and does
not factor in the payment of dividends by Silvercorp to its shareholders. The 
Company does take into account overall share price performance in determining 
executive compensation amounts; however, share price performance is just one of 
the many factors, as discussed above, that the Company takes into consideration.
Overall, the base salaries, or consulting fees, for the Named Executive Officers
have had an upward trend, however at a rate lower than the upward trend in the 
share performance graph below. However, there is not a direct correlation 
between the Company&#8217;s share price performance and the amount of 
compensation paid to Named Executive Officers.</FONT></P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><B><FONT color=#101010>Compensation of 
Directors</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Board of Directors has 
approved a Directors&#8217; compensation package that pays each non-executive
director CAD$41,250 per year. In addition, committee chairpersons are paid an 
additional CAD$8,250 per year, with the</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>19</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<A name="page_20"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Chairman of the Audit 
Committee receiving an additional CAD$24,750 per year. The Company has no formal
plans pursuant to which cash or non-cash compensation was paid or distributed to
executive officers for their roles as directors during the most recently 
completed financial year. The Compensation Committee reviews the 
Directors&#8217; compensation package on an annual basis and makes 
recommendations to the board of directors regarding director compensation when 
required.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>Total director compensation 
decreased to CAD$529,392 in fiscal 2013 compared to CAD$930,382 in fiscal 2012. 
The main reasons for the decrease were (i) in fiscal 2012, there were payments 
of CAD$178,800 to certain directors for acting as independent directors on a 
Special Committee formed in September 2011 to review the allegations issued by 
two anonymous sources in September respecting the Company&#8217;s financial 
position, no such fees were paid in fiscal 2013; (ii) the value of option-based 
awards decreased to CAD$290,142 in fiscal 2013 compared to CAD$469,926 in fiscal
2012; and (iii) bonuses of CAD$80,000 were paid to directors during fiscal 2012,
no such payments were made in fiscal 2013. The Company has no pension plan or 
other arrangement for non-cash compensation to the Directors, except 
Options.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The following table sets out 
compensation paid to directors in the financial year ended March 31, 
2013:</FONT></P>

<TD width="96%">
<P align=justify><FONT style="FONT-SIZE: 8pt" color=#101010>The Company has 
adopted IFRS 2 &#8211; Share Based Payments to account for the issuance of 
Options to employees and non-employees. The fair value of Options is estimated 
at the grant date using the Black-Scholes Option Pricing Model which requires 
the input of a number of assumptions. Although the assumptions used reflect 
management&#8217;s best estimates, they involve inherent uncertainties based on 
market conditions generally outside of the control of the Company. The following
summarizes the key assumption used to calculate the fair value of each set of 
Options granted to directors, who are not NEOs, during the financial year ended 
March 31, 2013:</FONT></P></TD></TR>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B><FONT color=#101010>SECURITIES AUTHORIZED FOR 
ISSUANCE</FONT></B><BR><B><FONT color=#101010>UNDER AND DESCRIPTION OF EQUITY 
COMPENSATION PLANS</FONT></B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The only equity compensation 
plan which the Company has in place is the Plan which was previously approved by
the shareholders on November 14, 2002, and amended by shareholders on October 
20, 2004, October 24, 2005, and August 24, 2006. At the 2009 annual general 
meeting, shareholders approved a new Amendment to the Plan in order to, amongst 
other things; convert the Plan into a &#8220;rolling 10% plan&#8221; from a 
&#8220;fixed number plan&#8221;. At the 2012 annual general meeting, 
shareholders re-approved the Plan. At March 31, 2013, there were 4,503,969 
Options</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>23</FONT></P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center width="100%" noShade SIZE=1>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_24"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-RIGHT: 0%; PADDING-LEFT: 0%;%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>outstanding (representing 
2.6% of the Company&#8217;s issued and outstanding Common Shares) and 12,574,137
Options available for future issuance under the Plan.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Plan has been established
to attract and retain directors, officers, employees and consultants to the
Company and to motivate them to advance the interests of the Company by 
affording them with the opportunity to acquire an equity interest in the 
Company. The Plan is administered by the directors and the Corporate Governance 
and Compensation Committee of the Company.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Board, or a committee 
appointed for such purposes, may from time to time designate, by resolution, to 
bona fide Employees, Consultants, Officers or Directors (collectively, the 
&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>Eligible Persons</FONT></B><FONT 
color=#101010>&#8221;), or corporations employing or wholly owned by such 
Eligible Persons options to acquire Common Shares in such numbers, for such 
terms and at such exercise prices as may be determined by the Board or such 
committee. The purpose of this Plan is to attract and retain Eligible Persons 
and to motivate them to advance the interests of the Company by affording them 
with the opportunity to acquire an equity interest in the Company through 
Options granted under the Plan to purchase Common Shares.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The maximum number of Common 
Shares that may be reserved for issuance for all purposes under the Plan is 10% 
of the issued and outstanding Common Shares, from time to time. Any Common 
Shares subject to an Option which for any reason is cancelled or terminated 
without having been exercised will again be available for grant under the Plan. 
Additionally if any Option has been exercised, the number of Common Shares into 
which such Option was exercised will become available to be issued upon the 
exercise of Options subsequently granted under the Plan. Thus upon exercise of 
an Option, the same number of Common Shares underlying those Options would 
become available for issuance under the Plan.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The maximum number of Common 
Shares under the Plan and any other share compensation arrangement of the 
Company (i) issued to Insiders within any one year period, and (ii) issuable to 
Insiders at any time, may not exceed 10% of the company's issued and outstanding
Common Shares. The maximum number of Common Shares issued to each Eligible 
Person under the Plan and under any other share compensation arrangement is 
limited to 5% of the Common Shares issued and outstanding at the time of the 
grant.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Board may from time to 
time, subject to applicable law and to the prior approval, if required, of the 
TSX or any other regulatory body having authority over the Company or the Plan 
or, if required by the rules and policies of the TSX, the approval of the 
shareholders of the Company, suspend, terminate or discontinue the Plan at any 
time, or amend or revise the terms of the Plan or of any Option granted under 
the Plan.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The Board has the authority 
under the Plan to establish the exercise price at the time each Option is 
granted. The exercise price of an Option may not be less than the closing market
price for the Company&#8217;s Shares on the TSX on the trading day prior to the 
date of grant of the Options. The Board, or a committee appointed for such 
purposes, also has the authority under the Plan to determine other terms and 
conditions relating to the grant of the Options, including any applicable 
vesting provisions. The Plan also includes a specific amending provision that 
details the amendments to the Plan that may be made by the Board of Directors 
without shareholder approval and that detail certain amendments to the Plan that
specifically require shareholder approval.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>The term of the Options 
granted under the Plan shall expire on a date determined by the Board, which may
not be later than 10 years from the date of grant of the Option. However, the 
Plan provides that Options that would otherwise expire during &#8220;no 
trading&#8221; periods (&#8220;</FONT><B><FONT color=#101010>Blackout 
Periods</FONT></B><FONT color=#101010>&#8221;) established by the Company will 
be extended for 10 business days after the Blackout Period expires.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><FONT color=#101010>All Options granted under the
Plan are not assignable or transferable other than by will or the laws of 
succession, except that, if permitted by the rules and policies of the TSX, an 
optionee shall have the right to assign any Option granted to a trust, RRSP, 
RESP or similar legal entity. If an optionee ceases to be an Eligible Person for
any reason whatsoever other than death, each Option held by such optionee will 
cease to be exercisable 90 days following the termination date (being the date 
on which such optionee ceases to be an Eligible Person). If an optionee dies, 
the legal representative of the optionee may exercise the optionee&#8217;s 
Options within one year after the date of the optionee&#8217;s death but only up
to and including the original Option expiry date.</FONT></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><FONT color=#101010>24</FONT></P></DIV><BR>

<P style="MARGIN: 0px">&nbsp;</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>INDEBTEDNESS OF DIRECTORS, EXECUTIVE OFFICERS 
<BR>AND SENIOR OFFICERS</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">During the Company's last completed financial 
year ended March 31, 2013, no director or executive officer of the Company, no 
proposed nominee for election as a director of the Company, and no associate of 
any of the foregoing persons has been indebted to the Company or any of its 
subsidiaries, nor has any of these individuals been indebted to another entity 
which indebtedness is the subject of a guarantee, support agreement, letter of 
credit or other similar arrangement or understanding provided by the Company or 
any of its subsidiaries.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>MANAGEMENT CONTRACTS</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">There are no management functions of the Company 
which are to any substantial degree performed by a person or company other than 
the directors or executive officers of the Company (or private companies 
controlled by them, either directly or indirectly).</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>INTEREST OF INFORMED PERSONS IN MATERIAL 
TRANSACTIONS</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Except as disclosed in this Information Circular,
since the commencement of the Company's most recently completed financial year, 
no informed person of the Company, nominee for election as a director or any 
associate or affiliate of an informed person or nominee, had any material 
interest, direct or indirect, in any transaction or any proposed transaction 
which has materially affected or would materially affect the Company or any of 
its subsidiaries. An &#8220;informed person&#8221; means: (a) a director or 
executive officer of the Company; (b) a director or executive officer of a 
person or company that is itself an informed person or subsidiary of the 
Company; (c) any person or company who beneficially owns, directly or 
indirectly, voting securities of the Company or who exercises control or 
direction over voting securities of the Company or a combination of both 
carrying more than 10% of the voting rights other than voting securities held by
the person or company as underwriter in the course of a distribution; and (d) 
the Company itself, if and for so long as, it has purchased, redeemed or 
otherwise acquired any of its Common Shares.</P>

hold office until the next annual general meeting of the shareholders of the 
Company or until a successor is appointed, and that the directors be authorized 
to determine the auditor&#8217;s remuneration. Deloitte LLP, Chartered 
Accountants was first appointed as the auditors of the Company on November 26, 
2012. Attached as <B>Appendix &#8220;B&#8221; </B>to this Information Circular
are copies of the Notice of Change in Auditor, Letter from Ernst &amp;</P>

<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>SCHEDULE &#8220;1&#8221;</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS CHARTER</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Board is responsible for the stewardship of 
the Company and for the oversight of its management and affairs.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Directors shall exercise their best business 
judgment in a manner consistent with their fiduciary duties. The Board&#8217;s 
primary responsibilities, which are discharged directly and through delegation 
to its Committees, include the following:</P>
<UL>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To act honestly and in good faith with a view to the best 
interests of the Company.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To exercise due care, diligence and skill that reasonably 
prudent persons would exercise in comparable circumstances.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>Consistent with its responsibilities to the Company, to further
the interests of the shareholders.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To consider business opportunities and risks, and to adopt 
strategic plans from time to time.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To identify the principal risks of the Company&#8217;s 
business, and to implement an appropriate system to manage these risks.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To develop an investor relations and shareholder communications
policy for the Company.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To oversee management&#8217;s adoption of effective internal 
control and management information systems.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review and approve annual and quarterly financial statements
and the publication thereof by management.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To approve operating plans and any capital budget plans.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To select and approve all key executive appointments, and to 
monitor executive development.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To develop the Company&#8217;s approach to corporate 
governance, including establishing a set of corporate governance principles and 
guidelines that are specifically applicable to the Company.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To adopt a code of conduct to govern employees and management 
in their activities for and on behalf of the Company.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To promote a culture of integrity throughout the Company 
consistent with the adopted code of conduct.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To take action on issues that by law or practice require the 
independent action of a Board or one of its Committees.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To oversee management in its implementation of effective 
programs to provide a safe work environment, to employ sound environmental 
practices, and to operate in accordance with applicable laws, regulations and 
permits.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To oversee management in its implementation of an effective 
communications policy with regard to investors, employees, the communities in 
which it operates and the governments of those communities.</P></LI></UL>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center">27</P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center SIZE=1 width="100%" noShade>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_4"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>SCHEDULE &#8220;2&#8221;</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>CORPORATE GOVERNANCE COMMITTEE CHARTER</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company has established a Corporate 
Governance Committee of the Board of Directors which consists of three or more 
directors, a majority of whom shall be independent. The Committee meets at least
annually, or more frequently as required.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee&#8217;s mandate is to assist the 
Board in establishing and maintaining a sound system of corporate governance 
through a process of continuing assessment and enhancement.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee&#8217;s duties and responsibilities
are:</P>
<UL>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To advise the Chairman of the Board and the Board on matters of
corporate governance, including adherence to any governance guidelines or rules 
established by applicable regulatory authorities.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To advise the Board on issues of conflict of interest for 
individual directors.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To examine the effectiveness of the Company&#8217;s corporate 
governance practices at least annually and to propose such procedures and 
policies as the Committee believes are appropriate to ensure that the Board 
functions independently of management, management is accountable to the Board 
and procedures are in place to monitor the effectiveness of performance of the 
Board, committees of the Board and individual directors.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To develop and review, together with the Chairman, CEO and the 
President of the Board, annual Board goals or improvement priorities.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To identify and to recommend to the Board suitable candidates 
for nomination as new directors, and to review the credentials of directors 
standing for re-election.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>With assistance of management, to organize and provide an 
orientation program for new directors where appropriate.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To periodically review the mandates of the Board and committees
of the Board and determine what additional committees of the Board, if any, are 
required or appropriate.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To develop such codes of conduct and other policies as are 
appropriate to deal with the confidentiality of the Company&#8217;s information,
insider trading and the Company&#8217;s timely disclosure and other public 
company obligations.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To take such other steps as the Committee decides are 
appropriate, in consultation with the Board, to ensure that proper corporate 
governance practices are in place for the Company, with reference to the Toronto
Stock Exchange guidelines or recommendations and other regulatory requirements 
on corporate governance.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review its charter and assess annually the adequacy of this 
mandate, the effectiveness of its performance and, when necessary, and to 
recommend changes to the Board of Directors for its approval.</P></LI></UL>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center">28</P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center SIZE=1 width="100%" noShade>
<BR>
<!--$$/page=--><A name="page_5"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>SCHEDULE &#8220;3&#8221;</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>COMPENSATION COMMITTEE CHARTER</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Compensation Committee of the Board of 
Directors consists of at least three Directors, a majority of whom shall be 
independent. The Committee meets at least annually, or more frequently as 
required.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The purpose of the Compensation Committee is to 
assist the Board in discharging its duties relating to compensation of the 
executive officers of the Company. The goals are to enable the Company to 
attract, retain and motivate the most qualified talent who will contribute to 
the long term success of the Company by aligning compensation with the 
Company&#8217;s business objectives and performance, and aligning incentives 
with the interests of shareholders to maximize shareholders&#8217; value.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee&#8217;s duties and responsibilities
are:</P>
<UL>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To make recommendations to the Board with respect to the 
compensation of senior management and executive officers of the Company.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review the compensation and benefits of the directors in 
their capacity as directors of the Company to ensure that such compensation 
reflects the responsibilities and risks involved in being a director.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review and make recommendations to the Board as to the 
general compensation and benefits policies and practices of the Company, 
including incentive stock options for all employees, consultants, directors and 
officers.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review the disclosure to be made of director and executive 
remuneration in the Management Information Circular.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To ensure there are appropriate training, development and 
benefit programs in place for management and staff.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review and make recommendations to the Board for its 
approval on any special compensation and benefit arrangements.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review its compensation practices by comparing them to 
surveys of relevant competitors and to set objective compensation based on this 
review.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To perform such other functions as the Board may from time to 
time assign to the Committee.</P>
<LI>
<P align=justify>To review its charter and assess annually the adequacy of this 
mandate, the effectiveness of its performance, and to recommend changes to the 
Board for its approval.</P></LI></UL>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center">29</P></DIV><BR>
<HR style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always" align=center SIZE=1 width="100%" noShade>
<BR>
<A name="page_6"></A><BR>
<DIV style="PADDING-LEFT: 0%; PADDING-RIGHT: 0%">
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>SCHEDULE &#8220;4&#8221;</B></P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><B>AUDIT COMMITTEE CHARTER</B></P>
<DIV align=left>
<TABLE style="WIDTH: 100%; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman'; FONT-SIZE: 10pt" 
border=0 cellSpacing=0>
<TR>
<TD width="4%"></TD>
<TD width="92%"></TD></TR>
<TR vAlign=bottom>
<TD noWrap align=left><B>I.</B></TD>
<TD noWrap align=left><B>Purpose</B></TD></TR></TABLE></DIV>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The main objective of the Audit Committee is to 
act as a liaison between the Board and the Company&#8217;s independent auditors 
(the &#8220;Auditors&#8221;) and to assist the Board in fulfilling its oversight
responsibilities with respect to (a) the financial statements and other 
financial information provided by the Company to its shareholders, the public 
and others; (b) the Company&#8217;s compliance with legal and regulatory 
requirements; (c) the qualification, independence and performance of the 
Auditors; and (d) the Company's risk management and internal financial and 
accounting controls, and management information systems.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Although the Committee has the powers and 
responsibilities set forth in this Charter, the role of the Committee is 
oversight. The members of the Committee are not full-time employees of the 
Company and may or may not be accountants or auditors by profession or experts 
in the fields of accounting or auditing and, in any event, do not serve in such 
capacity. Consequently, it is not the duty of the Committee to conduct audits or
to determine that the Company&#8217;s financial statements and disclosures are 
complete and accurate and are in accordance with generally accepted accounting 
principles and applicable rules and regulations.</P>
<DIV align=left>
<TABLE style="WIDTH: 100%; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman'; FONT-SIZE: 10pt" 
border=0 cellSpacing=0>
<TR>
<TD width="4%"></TD>
<TD width="92%"></TD></TR>
<TR vAlign=bottom>
<TD noWrap align=left><B>II.</B></TD>
<TD noWrap align=left><B>Organization</B></TD></TR></TABLE></DIV>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee shall consist of three or more 
directors and shall satisfy the laws governing the Company and the independence,
financial literacy, expertise and experience requirements under applicable 
securities law, stock exchange and any other regulatory requirements applicable 
to the Company.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The members of the Committee and the Chair of the
Committee shall be appointed by the Board. A majority of the members of the 
Committee shall constitute a quorum. A majority of the members of the Committee 
shall be empowered to act on behalf of the Committee. Matters decided by the 
Committee shall be decided by majority votes.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Any member of the Committee may be removed or 
replaced at any time by the Board and shall cease to be a member of the 
Committee as soon as such member ceases to be a director.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee may form and delegate authority to 
subcommittees when appropriate.</P>
<DIV align=left>
<TABLE style="WIDTH: 100%; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman'; FONT-SIZE: 10pt" 
border=0 cellSpacing=0>
<TR>
<TD width="4%"></TD>
<TD width="92%"></TD></TR>
<TR vAlign=bottom>
<TD noWrap align=left><B>III.</B></TD>
<TD noWrap align=left><B>Meetings</B></TD></TR></TABLE></DIV>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee shall meet as frequently as 
circumstances require, but not less frequently than four times per year. The 
Committee shall meet at least quarterly.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Committee may invite, from time to time, such
persons as it may see fit to attend its meetings and to take part in discussion 
and consideration of the affairs of the Committee.</P>
<P style="TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company&#8217;s accounting and financial 
officer(s) and the Auditors shall attend any meeting when requested to do so by 
the Chair of the Committee.</P>

hiring policies regarding partners, employees and  former partners and employees
of the present and former external auditor of the issuer.</P></TD></TR>

<P> The Company provides new directors with an  orientation program upon 
joining the Company that  includes copies of relevant financial, technical,  
geological and other information regarding its<BR> properties, as well as 
meetings with management.  Board members are encouraged to communicate with  
management and auditors, to keep themselves current  with industry trends and 
developments, and to attend  related industry seminars. The Company may also  
request that </P>

their  conduct, duties and responsibilities. Individual board  members, the 
Corporate Secretary, and In-house  Counsel from time to time attend continuing  
education courses to stay abreast of latest  developments in corporate 
governance and  regulatory compliance issues.<BR></P></TD></TR>

and for overseeing  and monitoring compliance with the Code. The  Code also sets
out mechanisms for the reporting of  unethical conduct.<BR><BR> The Code is 
applicable to all employees, consultants,  officers and directors, regardless of
their position  with the Company, at all times and everywhere the  Company does 
business. The Code provides that the  Company&#8217;s employees, consultants,
officers and  directors will uphold its commitment to a culture of  honesty, 
integrity and accountability.<BR><BR> The Board has not granted any waiver of 
the Code in  favor of a director or executive officer, and no  material change 
report has been required or filed in  connection with the Code.<BR><BR> When 
proposed transactions or agreements in which  directors or officers may have an 
interest, material or  not, are presented to the Board, the directors are  
required to disclose any such interest and the persons  who have such an 
interest are excluded from all  discussion on the matter and are not permitted 
to vote  on the proposal. All such interests in transactions or  agreements 
involving senior management are dealt  with by the Board, regardless of apparent
immateriality.<BR><BR> The Board also adopted a formal &#8220;Code of Ethical  
Conduct for Financial Managers&#8221; that is applicable to  all Financial 
Managers of the Company, being the  Company&#8217;s Chief Executive Officer, 
Chief Financial  Officer, principal accounting officer, controller and  persons 
performing similar functions.<BR><BR> Further, the Board approved and 
implemented a  &#8220;Whistle Blower&#8221; process available to all directors, 
officers, employees, and any other party. The Chair  of the Audit Committee 
monitors and reports any  wrong doing to the Audit Committee. For the

candidates.<BR></TD></TR>
